  A customer-facing order may include multiple legs across countries, for

  Canada leg                                                                    
  US leg

  multi-stop and multi-move execution inside a single shipment                  
  split pickup / split delivery patterns                                        
  inter-organization EDI load tender transfers, where one organization can send 
  a shipment tender to another organization, the target organization creates    
  its own shipment, and both shipments are linked for status synchronization    
  Because of that, I want to confirm whether multi-leg / multi-entity workflows 
  are expected to be modeled in one of these existing ways, instead of through  
  an order aggregate.                                                           
                                                                                
  What I have not found so far:                                                 
                                                                                
  a top-level order entity above shipment                                       
  order -> many shipments modeling                                              
  one customer invoice covering multiple shipments/legs

  per-leg supplier/entity execution under one commercial order                  
  I also noticed:                                                               
                                                                                
  invoices are tied to a single shipment_id                                     
  billing queue items are tied to a single shipment_id                          
  CreateFromShipments rejects grouped invoices with ‚ÄúGrouped invoices are not   
  supported yet‚ÄĚ                                                                
  there are invoice summary / consolidation-related fields, but I could not     
  find an end-to-end grouped invoice implementation                             
  Questions:                                                                    
                                                                                
  Is the recommended modeling approach for multi-country / multi-leg workflows: 
  one shipment with multiple moves/stops,                                       
  inter-organization EDI transfers between organizations,                       
  or is there another intended pattern?                                         
  Are inter-org EDI transfers the intended way to model one commercial movement 
  executed by different company entities or operating organizations?            
  If so, how is customer-facing commercial continuity supposed to be handled:   
  one quote,                                                                    
  one order,                                                                    
  one invoice,

‚óŹ Here's the answer based on a full read of the codebase.

  Short version

  The user's read of the code is essentially correct. Trenova today supports the
  execution primitives for multi-leg cross-border movements, but not the
  commercial aggregate they're describing. There is no order-above-shipment, no
  order-level AR, no grouped invoice, no route/customs aggregate, and no
  external carrier/supplier cost. What looks like "consolidation" in the schema
  is load consolidation (operational grouping of shipments for dispatch), not
  the commercial order concept they want ‚ÄĒ and even that is schema-only
  scaffolding.

  What exists today (their read is accurate)

  Multi-leg execution ‚ÄĒ fully supported. The hierarchy is Shipment ‚Üí 
  ShipmentMove ‚Üí Stop ‚Üí Assignment. Each move is an independently-assignable leg
  (its own driver/tractor/trailer via Assignment), over an ordered set of
  stops. A CA‚ÜíUS‚ÜíMX journey can be modeled as one shipment with three moves.
  Split pickup/delivery are just StopType values (Pickup, SplitPickup, Delivery,
  SplitDelivery) ‚ÄĒ no separate entity.
  - domain/shipment/{shipment.go, shipmentmove.go, stop.go, assignment.go}

  Inter-org EDI load tender transfers ‚ÄĒ fully built. EDITransfer
  (edi_load_tender_transfers) carries source/target org+shipment, a JSONB
  LoadTenderPayload, and a MappingSnapshot that remaps source entity IDs into
  the target org's IDs. On approval it creates the target org's shipment and a
  ShipmentLink (edi_shipment_links) with a SyncPolicy and per-domain
  FieldOwnership (source owns billing/rating/charges; target owns
  dispatch/actuals). Bidirectional status/lifecycle sync runs through
  internaledistatussync (event mirroring) and internaledilifecycle
  (stop-actual/status apply + conflict detection). This is explicitly designed
  for multiple organizations under one BusinessUnit ‚ÄĒ internal partners carry
  InternalOrganizationID and there's a ConnectionMethodInternal transport
  shortcut.
  - domain/edi/{transfer.go, sync.go, tenderchange.go, partner.go},
  services/ediservice/service.go:816-991

  Tenant hierarchy ‚ÄĒ two levels, no nesting. BusinessUnit (the group) ‚Üí
  Organization (operating company / legal entity, with its own ScacCode,
  DOTNumber, TaxID). No ParentID on either.

  What does NOT exist (confirming their gaps)

  Concept they want: Order aggregate above shipment
  Status: None. Shipment is the top operational entity. No Order domain.
  ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ
  Concept they want: order ‚Üí many shipments
  Status: None.
  ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ
  Concept they want: One invoice covering multiple shipments
  Status: None. Invoice.ShipmentID and BillingQueueItem.ShipmentID are single,
  non-null FKs. Strictly 1 shipment ‚Üí 1 queue item ‚Üí 1 invoice.
  ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ
  Concept they want: CreateFromShipments grouping
  Status: Blocked. Signature takes ShipmentIDs []pulid.ID but hard-rejects len >
   
  1 with "Grouped invoices are not supported yet"
  (invoiceservice/delivery.go:93-95), then only processes [0].
  ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ
  Concept they want: Route aggregate w/ customs/border checkpoints
  Status: None. "Route" is only distance metadata on a move
  (DistanceRouteSignature, etc.). No checkpoint entity.
  ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ
  Concept they want: Per-leg supplier/carrier cost
  Status: None. Asset-based model only (worker/tractor/trailer). No
  carrier/supplier/vendor entity, no buy-side cost field ‚ÄĒ all shipment money
  is revenue-side (FreightChargeAmount, BaseRate, TotalChargeAmount). Only
  carrier-cost artifact is inbound EDI 210 parsing.

  The "consolidation" fields are a red herring for their use case. There are two
  unrelated consolidation concepts, both incomplete:
  1. Load consolidation ‚ÄĒ Shipment.ConsolidationGroupID +
  consolidation_groups/consolidation_settings tables + customer flags
  (AllowConsolidation, etc.). This is operational (group nearby loads onto one
  truck), not commercial. And it's schema + settings only ‚ÄĒ no Go domain entity,
  repository, or service logic. It's an ID passthrough in the GraphQL resolver.
  2. Invoice consolidation ‚ÄĒ BillingProfile.{AllowInvoiceConsolidation, 
  ConsolidationPeriodDays, ConsolidationGroupBy} and
  Customer.{AllowConsolidation, ExclusiveConsolidation, ConsolidationPriority}.
  These are config placeholders ‚ÄĒ nothing reads them to actually produce a
  multi-shipment invoice.

  So yes: the summary/consolidation fields are placeholders for future grouped
  billing, not a working implementation.

  Answering their questions directly

  1. Recommended way to model multi-country/multi-leg today? For a single
  commercial movement executed by one org: one shipment with multiple
  moves/stops. For a movement executed by different legal entities/orgs in the
  same group: inter-org EDI transfers. There is no third intended pattern, and
  no order aggregate to hang them under.
  2. Are inter-org EDI transfers the intended way to model one commercial 
  movement across entities? Operationally, yes ‚ÄĒ that's exactly what
  ShipmentLink + field ownership are for. But they link shipments for
  status/data sync, not for commercial rollup. There is no shared commercial
  parent.
  3. How is customer-facing commercial continuity handled (one 
  quote/order/invoice over many internal shipments)? It currently isn't. Each
  shipment bills independently. There's no order, no order-level AR, no grouped
  invoice.
  4. Any business object above shipment for order-level AR / per-leg vendor 
  cost? No.
  5. Are consolidation/summary settings placeholders? Yes ‚ÄĒ placeholders, not
  implemented end-to-end.

  Recommended extension path

  I'd frame it to them as three separable layers, buildable independently, in
  priority order:

  1. Commercial Order aggregate (the core gap). New domain/order entity: one
  Order ‚Üí many Shipment (add nullable Shipment.OrderID). Order holds the
  customer, quoted/base amount, and order-level charges. Shipments remain the
  execution unit (one per leg/entity). This is the single highest-leverage
  addition and unblocks everything else. The existing per-move charge model and
  AdditionalCharge already give you the "base + extras" pricing they mention.

  2. Grouped invoicing at the order level. This is the biggest data-model change
  because shipment_id is currently non-null on both Invoice and
  BillingQueueItem. Path: move shipment attribution off the invoice header onto
  invoice lines (or a junction), add Invoice.OrderID, remove the len > 1 guard
  in CreateFromShipments, and wire the already-present ConsolidationGroupBy /
  AllowInvoiceConsolidation settings into the queue‚Üíinvoice builder. The
  ShipmentIDs []pulid.ID signature already anticipates this.

  3. Route / customs checkpoints + buy-side cost (only if the use case needs 
  them). A Route aggregate with first-class border/customs checkpoints, and a
  carrier/supplier + per-leg cost model, are genuinely new domains (Trenova has
  neither). These are the largest lifts and I'd defer them unless the
  cross-border customs workflow or carrier settlement is actually in scope ‚ÄĒ
  they can bolt onto the Order aggregate later.

  Net: don't overload load-consolidation or EDI transfers to fake a commercial
  order. Build the Order aggregate (layer 1) first; it's the missing keystone,
  and layers 2‚Äď3 are additive once it exists.

  Want me to draft an issue reply, or scope out the Order aggregate (layer 1) as
  an implementation plan?

‚óŹ Drafted below (also saved to scratchpad/issue-reply.md).

  ---
  Thanks for the detailed writeup ‚ÄĒ your reading of the code is accurate, and
  you've correctly identified where the boundaries are. Let me confirm the
  intended architecture and answer each question directly.

  Short answer

  Trenova today supports the execution primitives for multi-leg cross-border
  movements, but not the commercial aggregate you're describing. There is
  intentionally no order-above-shipment, no order-level AR, no grouped invoice,
  and no route/customs aggregate. The consolidation_* schema you found is load 
  consolidation (operational grouping for dispatch), not commercial order
  aggregation ‚ÄĒ and it's currently schema/settings scaffolding only.

  What is intended today

  - Multi-leg / multi-stop within one shipment ‚ÄĒ first class. The hierarchy is
  Shipment ‚Üí ShipmentMove ‚Üí Stop ‚Üí Assignment. Each move is an
  independently-assignable leg (its own driver/tractor/trailer), over an ordered
  set of stops. A CA‚ÜíUS‚ÜíMX journey executed by one org is one shipment with
  three moves. Split pickup/delivery are StopType values (Pickup, SplitPickup,
  Delivery, SplitDelivery), not separate entities.
  - Inter-org EDI load tender transfers ‚ÄĒ first class, for movements executed by
  different legal entities/organizations within the same business unit.
  EDITransfer creates the target org's shipment and a ShipmentLink with a
  SyncPolicy and per-domain FieldOwnership (source owns billing/rating/charges;
  target owns dispatch/actuals). Status and lifecycle sync bidirectionally.

  Answers to your specific questions

  1. Recommended modeling for multi-country / multi-leg?
  - One org executing the whole journey ‚Üí one shipment with multiple 
  moves/stops.
  - Different legal entities/orgs in the same group executing legs ‚Üí inter-org 
  EDI transfers, one shipment per executing entity, linked via ShipmentLink.
  - There is no third intended pattern, and no order aggregate to group them
  under.

  2. Are inter-org EDI transfers the intended way to model one commercial 
  movement across entities?
  Operationally, yes ‚ÄĒ ShipmentLink + field ownership exist exactly for this.
  But they link shipments for status/data synchronization, not commercial
  rollup. There is no shared commercial parent above the linked shipments.

  3. How is customer-facing commercial continuity (one quote / order / invoice 
  over many internal shipments) handled?
  Today it isn't. Each shipment bills independently:
  - Invoice.ShipmentID and BillingQueueItem.ShipmentID are single, non-null FKs
  ‚ÄĒ strictly 1 shipment ‚Üí 1 billing queue item ‚Üí 1 invoice.
  - CreateFromShipments takes ShipmentIDs []pulid.ID but hard-rejects len > 1
  ("Grouped invoices are not supported yet") and processes only the first. That
  plural signature is a forward-looking placeholder, not a working path.

  4. Any business object above shipment for order-level AR or per-leg 
  supplier/vendor cost?
  No. There is no order aggregate, no order-level AR, and no buy-side cost
  model. Trenova is asset-based (worker/tractor/trailer) ‚ÄĒ there is no
  carrier/supplier/vendor entity and no per-leg cost field. All monetary fields
  on a shipment are revenue-side (FreightChargeAmount, BaseRate,
  TotalChargeAmount). The only carrier-cost artifact is inbound EDI 210 parsing.

  5. Are the consolidation / summary invoice settings placeholders?
  Yes. Two unrelated consolidation concepts exist, both incomplete:
  - Load consolidation ‚ÄĒ Shipment.ConsolidationGroupID +
  consolidation_groups/consolidation_settings tables + customer flags.
  Operational (group nearby loads onto one truck), and currently schema +
  settings only ‚ÄĒ no domain entity/repository/service logic behind it yet.
  - Invoice consolidation ‚ÄĒ BillingProfile.{AllowInvoiceConsolidation, 
  ConsolidationPeriodDays, ConsolidationGroupBy} and the Customer consolidation
  flags. Config placeholders ‚ÄĒ nothing reads them to actually produce a
  multi-shipment invoice.

  So neither the load-consolidation FK nor the invoice-consolidation settings
  should be treated as a hook for the commercial order concept you're after.

  Recommended extension path

  I'd build this as three separable layers, in priority order. Please don't
  overload load-consolidation or EDI transfers to fake a commercial order ‚ÄĒ
  those solve different problems.

  Layer 1 ‚ÄĒ Commercial Order aggregate (the keystone). A new domain/order
  entity: one Order ‚Üí many Shipment (add nullable Shipment.OrderID). The order
  holds the customer, the quoted/base amount, and order-level charges; shipments
  stay the execution unit (one per leg / executing entity). This is the single
  highest-leverage addition and unblocks everything else. The existing per-move
  charge model and AdditionalCharge already give you the "base + extras" pricing
  you described.

  Layer 2 ‚ÄĒ Grouped invoicing at the order level. This is the larger data-model
  change, because shipment_id is non-null on both Invoice and BillingQueueItem.
  Path: move shipment attribution off the invoice header onto invoice lines (or
  a junction table), add Invoice.OrderID, drop the len > 1 guard in
  CreateFromShipments, and wire the existing ConsolidationGroupBy /
  AllowInvoiceConsolidation settings into the queue‚Üíinvoice builder. The
  ShipmentIDs slice already anticipates this.

  Layer 3 ‚ÄĒ Route / customs checkpoints and buy-side cost (only if in scope). A
  Route aggregate with first-class border/customs checkpoints, plus a
  carrier/supplier entity and per-leg cost model, are genuinely new domains
  (Trenova has neither today). These are the largest lifts; defer them unless
  the cross-border customs workflow or carrier settlement is actually part of
  your use case. They bolt onto the Order aggregate cleanly later.

  Net recommendation: build the Order aggregate (Layer 1) first ‚ÄĒ it's the
  missing keystone ‚ÄĒ then Layers 2 and 3 are additive. Happy to help scope Layer
  1 if you'd like to open a design discussion.

      7 ## 1. The one-sentence definition
      9 An **order aggregate** is a single commercial entity that sits **

‚óŹ Written to docs/design/order-aggregate.md. It covers:

  1. One-sentence definition + the shipment-does-two-jobs framing (commercial
  vs. operational split) with a diagram.
  2. What "aggregate" means in DDD ‚ÄĒ aggregate root, consistency boundary,
  identity/lifecycle ‚ÄĒ and how Order/Shipment/OrderCharge map onto
  root/entity/value-object, including the "reference other aggregates by ID"
  nuance for why shipment stays its own root.
  3. Why the shipment can't keep doing this ‚ÄĒ mapped to the actual code gaps
  (invoice/billing FKs, CreateFromShipments guard, EDI links, why
  ConsolidationGroupID is the wrong tool).
  4. Concrete Order struct following your exact conventions (composite tenant
  PK, PULID, epoch int64, decimal.NullDecimal, Version, bun rel tags) + the
  single nullable OrderID FK on shipment.
  5. Status lifecycle, the invariants the root enforces (the part that actually
  makes it an aggregate), composition with existing machinery
  (EDI/consolidation/billing) with a full cross-border walkthrough, non-goals,
  and a closing mental model.

  The struct/lifecycle are illustrative, not prescriptive ‚ÄĒ flagged as a design
  exploration. Want me to turn this into an implementation plan for Layer 1, or
  add a schema/migration sketch?

     Order Aggregate ‚ÄĒ Implementation Plan

     Context

     A GitHub evaluator asked whether Trenova can model multi-country /
     multi-leg cross-border movements as one commercial order spanning many
     shipments, with order-level AR and a single invoice covering all legs. It
     can't today: the shipment is both the thing you sell and the thing a truck 
     executes. There is no entity above shipment, invoices/billing-queue items
     are strictly 1:1 with a shipment (CreateFromShipments hard-rejects len>1),
     and "consolidation" in the schema is load consolidation (dispatch
     grouping), not commercial aggregation.

     This introduces an Order aggregate root that owns the commercial layer
     (customer, quote, AR rollup, status) while shipments remain the execution
     unit (one per leg). Design rationale is in docs/design/order-aggregate.md.

     Scope decided with the user (maximal):
     - Full Order CRUD aggregate + nullable Shipment.OrderID link.
     - Auto-derive Order.status from child shipment statuses via the shipment
     event/observer system.
     - Auto-create a 1-leg order whenever a shipment is created with no order,
     plus a backfill for existing shipments.
     - Grouped invoicing: one invoice per order across many legs (lift the len>1
     guard, add Invoice.OrderID, attribute lines per leg).

     This is a large, multi-subsystem feature (~22 backend files/generators +
     ~10 client files + 3 cross-cutting mechanisms), not a small add. It follows
     the well-established servicetype vertical-slice pattern for the CRUD
     portions.

     ---
     Reference patterns (read before writing)

     - Backend CRUD slice (canonical): servicetype ‚ÄĒ domain
     internal/core/domain/servicetype/servicetype.go, port
     internal/core/ports/repositories/servicetype.go, repo internal/infrastructu
     re/postgres/repositories/servicetyperepository/servicetype.go,
     service+validator internal/core/services/servicetypeservice/, REST
     internal/api/handlers/servicetypehandler/handler.go, GraphQL
     internal/api/graphql/schema/service_type.graphqls +
     resolver/service_type.resolvers.go + resolver/servicetypemapping.go.
     - Nullable FK field style: Shipment.ConsolidationGroupID at shipment.go:70
     (exact shape for OrderID).
     - Shipment event observer (Mechanism A model):
     internaledistatussync/service.go ‚ÄĒ copy its Params/Observer/New shape, tx
     idiom, and out-of-tx realtime publish.
     - Sequence registration (for OrderNumber): SequenceTypeConsolidation across
     tenant/enums.go, tenant/sequencecatalog.go, pkg/seqgen/types.go,
     pkg/seqgen/generator.go.
     - Client CRUD slice: service-type ‚ÄĒ client/src/types/service-type.ts,
     client/src/graphql/operations/service-type/table.graphql,
     client/src/lib/graphql/service-type-table.ts,
     client/src/routes/service-type/.

     ---
     Backend

     Step 1 ‚ÄĒ Order domain + sequence plumbing (foundation)

     New package internal/core/domain/order/:
     - order.go ‚ÄĒ Order struct following Shipment/Customer conventions:
     composite tenant PK (id,business_unit_id,organization_id),
     pagination.CursorValueSet embed, CustomerID (notnull), OrderNumber
     (notnull), Status (enum, default Draft),
     QuotedAmount/BaseAmount/TotalAmount as decimal.NullDecimal, CurrencyCode,
     PONumber/BOL (nullzero), OwnerID/EnteredByID, Version, epoch
     CreatedAt/UpdatedAt. Relations: BusinessUnit,Organization,Customer
     belongs-to; Shipments []*shipment.Shipment has-many join:id=order_id.
     BeforeAppendModel mints pulid.MustNew("ord_"). Getters,
     GetPostgresSearchConfig, ozzo Validate.
     - status.go ‚ÄĒ OrderStatus enum
     (Draft/Confirmed/InProgress/Completed/Billed/Closed/Canceled) and the pure
     Derive(current OrderStatus, legs []shipment.Status) OrderStatus function
     (single source of truth for derivation, unit-testable). Rules:
     all-canceled‚ÜíCanceled (canceled legs otherwise excluded); all
     Invoiced‚ÜíBilled; all in {ReadyToInvoice,Completed,Invoiced}‚ÜíCompleted; any
     moving/mixed‚ÜíInProgress; all New‚ÜíConfirmed; zero legs‚ÜíDraft. Closed is
     terminal, never auto-set.
     - fieldmap_gen.go ‚ÄĒ generated by colgen.

     Sequence (OrderNumber, prefix "O"):
     - internal/core/domain/tenant/enums.go ‚ÄĒ add SequenceTypeOrder.
     - internal/core/domain/tenant/sequencecatalog.go ‚ÄĒ add to
     requiredSequenceTypes, the sort map, and a case SequenceTypeOrder: in
     DefaultSequenceFormat.
     - pkg/seqgen/types.go + pkg/seqgen/generator.go ‚ÄĒ add GenerateOrderNumber
     (copy GenerateConsolidationNumber).

     Permissions:
     - internal/core/domain/permission/resource_gen.go ‚ÄĒ add ResourceOrder 
     Resource = "order".
     - internal/core/domain/permission/registry.go ‚ÄĒ register ResourceDefinition
     (standardOps) in the appropriate register*Resources() group.

     Step 2 ‚ÄĒ Order repository + service + API (standard slice)

     - internal/core/ports/repositories/order.go ‚ÄĒ request DTOs +
     OrderRepository interface. Beyond the standard
     List/ListConnection/GetByID/GetByIDs/Create/Update/SelectOptions, add the
     methods the mechanisms need: UpdateStatus(ctx, req) (optimistic-version
     status write), GetShipmentStatuses(ctx, ti, orderID) []shipment.Status, and
     CreateInTx(ctx, tx, *order.Order) (narrow method used by the shipment repo
     to avoid a repo‚Üírepo cycle).
     - internal/infrastructure/postgres/repositories/orderrepository/order.go ‚ÄĒ
     Bun impl, tenant scoping via generated pkg/buncolgen/order_gen.go helpers,
     optimistic Version on Update/UpdateStatus (copy shipmentrepository
     pattern).
     - internal/core/services/orderservice/service.go + validator.go ‚ÄĒ
     transform‚Üívalidate‚Üírepo + audit, NewTenantedValidatorBuilder with unique
     order_number.
     - REST internal/api/handlers/orderhandler/handler.go
     (writes/list/select-options), GraphQL
     internal/api/graphql/schema/order.graphqls + resolver/order.resolvers.go
     (fill generated stub) + resolver/ordermapping.go + add OrderService to
     resolver/resolver.go Params/struct/constructor.
     - FX wiring: bootstrap/modules/repositories.go,
     bootstrap/modules/validators.go, bootstrap/modules/api/services.go,
     bootstrap/modules/api/handlers.go.
     - (Optional) seed under internal/infrastructure/database/seeds/ +
     regenerate.

     Step 3 ‚ÄĒ Migration: orders table + shipment link + backfill

     New pair internal/infrastructure/postgres/migrations/<ts>_orders_and_shipme
     nt_order_fk.tx.up.sql / .down.sql:
     - CREATE TABLE orders (composite PK, FKs to business_units/organizations ON
     DELETE CASCADE, version, epoch defaults, unique index on
     lower(order_number), organization_id, tenant/created indexes, search_vector
     + GIN).
     - ALTER TABLE shipments ADD COLUMN order_id VARCHAR(100) nullable + FK +
     index.
     - Backfill, one order per existing shipment (faithful 1:1): add a temporary
     orders.backfill_shipment_id column; INSERT INTO orders (... 
     backfill_shipment_id) SELECT ... FROM shipments WHERE order_id IS NULL
     minting ids as CONCAT('ord_', replace(gen_random_uuid()::text,'-',''))
     (precedent:
     20260528120000_register_accounting_control_permissions.tx.up.sql) and order
     numbers with a distinct 'O-BF-'||lpad(...) prefix (avoids colliding with
     runtime GenerateOrderNumber, no sequence-counter reconciliation needed);
     UPDATE shipments SET order_id = o.id FROM orders o WHERE 
     o.backfill_shipment_id = shipments.id; ALTER TABLE orders DROP COLUMN 
     backfill_shipment_id.
     - Also add the Mechanism-C columns here (see Step¬†6) so all schema lands
     together.

     Step 4 ‚ÄĒ Mechanism B: auto-create 1-leg order on shipment create

     In shipmentrepository/shipment.go Create (:356): the method already
     generates the pro number before opening the existing db.WithTx and inserts
     the shipment inside it. When entity.OrderID.IsNil(), mint an OrderNumber
     before the tx (same lifecycle as pro number ‚ÄĒ a rolled-back tx burns a
     number, consistent with today), then inside the existing tx call
     orderCreator.CreateInTx(tx, newOrder) (customer copied from shipment,
     status Confirmed), set entity.OrderID = newOrder.ID before the shipment
     insert. Add orderCreator + generator.GenerateOrderNumber to the repo
     constructor deps. shipmentservice.Create is structurally unchanged;
     returned shipment now carries OrderID.

     Shipment domain: add OrderID pulid.ID (nullzero, near :70) + Order 
     *order.Order belongs-to (near :105). GraphQL shipment.graphqls: add
     orderId: ID + order: Order + orderId to input ShipmentInput.

     Step 5 ‚ÄĒ Mechanism A: order status auto-derivation

     New observer package internal/core/services/orderderivation/ (service.go,
     service_test.go) implementing services.ShipmentEventObserver (interface at
     internal/core/ports/services/shipmentevent.go). On each shipment event:
     load the shipment, skip if OrderID nil, else recomputeOrder in a db.WithTx
     ‚ÄĒ read the order (with Version), skip if Closed, read all sibling leg
     statuses (orderRepo.GetShipmentStatuses), compute order.Derive(...), and
     UpdateStatus only if changed, guarded by optimistic Version with a bounded
     retry on version/serialization conflict
     (dberror.MapRetryableTransactionError). Publish orders/updated realtime
     invalidation out-of-tx. No loop risk: the observer writes only orders,
     never records a shipment event.

     Register in bootstrap/modules/api/services.go immediately after the
     internaledistatussync block, via fx.Annotate(orderderivation.New, 
     fx.As(new(services.ShipmentEventObserver)), 
     fx.ResultTags(\group:"shipment_event_observers"`))`.

     Ensure derivationRelevant includes the ShipmentCreated event and
     status-change events (emitted by
     shipmentservice/shipment_mutation_effects.go:emitStatusChangeEvent), so the
     Invoiced transition from Mechanism C drives the order to Billed.

     Step 6 ‚ÄĒ Mechanism C: grouped invoicing (one invoice per order)

     Schema (fold into Step 3 migration): invoices add order_id (nullable),
     order_number (nullable, denormalized), make shipment_id nullable;
     invoice_lines add shipment_id + shipment_pro_number + shipment_bol
     (nullable) so each line attributes to a leg; billing_queue_items add
     order_id (nullable; keep shipment_id notnull, one BQI per leg).

     Domain (internal/core/domain/invoice/invoice.go,
     billingqueue/billingqueue.go):
     - Invoice: add OrderID, OrderNumber, Order rel; ShipmentID ‚Üí nullzero.
     Validate: require ShipmentID or OrderID (either/or), keep ‚Č•1 line.
     - InoviceLine: add ShipmentID/ShipmentProNumber/ShipmentBOL; Validate
     requires per-line ShipmentID when the parent invoice has an OrderID.
     - BillingQueueItem: add OrderID.

     Service (invoiceservice/service.go, delivery.go) ‚ÄĒ additive, single-leg
     path preserved:
     - Generalize buildInvoiceLines ‚Üí buildInvoiceLinesForShipment(billType, 
     shp, startLineNumber) stamping leg attribution; single-leg caller passes
     startLineNumber=1.
     - New buildInvoiceEntityForOrder(anchorBQI, ord, legs, cus, control):
     iterate legs (deterministic sort), append lines with a running line number,
     set OrderID/OrderNumber, ShipmentID=nil; reuse
     syncInvoiceTotalsFromLines+SyncMinorAmounts unchanged. Header
     BillingQueueItemID points at the first leg's anchor BQI (keeps idempotency
     getExistingInvoiceByBillingQueueItem working); extend
     markBillingQueueItemPosted to mark all BQIs sharing the invoice's OrderID.
     - New CreateFromOrder(ctx, req, actor): load order + all shipments, filter
     billable legs (ReadyToInvoice/Completed), reject zero-billable and
     mixed-CustomerID, per-leg ExistsByShipmentAndType guard, one invoice
     number, one BQI per leg (same OrderID), build one invoice, validate,
     repo.Create, audit+realtime.
     - Lift the len>1 guard by delegation: in CreateFromShipments
     (delivery.go:93), when len>1 resolve the common order and delegate to
     CreateFromOrder (error if legs don't share one order); single-shipment
     branch untouched.

     Ports/API: add CreateInvoiceFromOrderRequest + CreateFromOrder to
     internal/core/ports/services/invoice.go (regenerate mock); REST route POST 
     /invoices/from-order/ in invoicehandler/handler.go; GraphQL
     invoice.graphqls add orderId/order/orderNumber to Invoice, make shipmentId
     nullable, add per-line fields (invoice creation stays REST).

     Codegen / build (run in order after edits)

     cd services/tms
     go generate ./internal/infrastructure/database/colgen/...   # buncolgen:
     order_gen.go + fieldmap_gen.go
     task gqlgen                                                  #
     generated.go, models_gen.go, *.resolvers.go stubs
     go generate ./internal/api/graphql/projection/...           # specs_gen.go
     (order spec)
     task generate-seeds                                         # only if a
     seed was added
     task lint && task test
     task db-migrate                                             # apply orders
     + backfill + invoice columns

     Client

     2. client/src/graphql/operations/order/table.graphql ‚ÄĒ OrderTable($input:

     defineDataTableGraphQLConfig<Order, OrderTableQueryVariables>({ document:

     ---
     Verification (end-to-end)

     1. Unit: order.Derive table-driven test (all-canceled, mixed, all-invoiced,
     all-new, empty) in orderderivation/order package.
     2. Migration + backfill: task db-reset; confirm every pre-existing shipment
     now has order_id and an O-BF- order; orders.backfill_shipment_id dropped.
     3. Auto-order: task run-watch, create a shipment via API/UI ‚Üí response has
     OrderID; a Confirmed order exists with OrderNumber O‚Ä¶.
     4. Derivation: advance the shipment through statuses (assign ‚Üí in transit ‚Üí
     deliver ‚Üí ready-to-invoice) and confirm the parent order derives
     Confirmed‚ÜíInProgress‚ÜíCompleted; cancel the leg ‚Üí order Canceled.
     5. Multi-leg + grouped invoice: create an order, attach 2‚Äď3 shipments
     (OrderID set), drive all to ReadyToInvoice, call POST /invoices/from-order/
     ‚Üí one invoice, OrderID set, lines attributed per leg with correct pro
     numbers, totals = sum of legs; legs move to Invoiced and order derives to
     Billed. Confirm single-leg CreateFromShipments still works unchanged.
     6. Client: order list/create/edit works; shipment shows its order; invoice
     shows order + per-leg lines. task lint, task test, npx tsc -b --force
     green.
     7. Optionally drive the app with the run / verify skills.

     ---
     Risks / edge cases

     - Backfill mapping needs the temp backfill_shipment_id column (CTE
     INSERT...RETURNING can't carry the source shipment id); keep it inside the
     one transactional migration and drop the column at the end. Add
     shipments.order_id FK after backfill (or nullable-then-tighten).
     - Order-number collision: backfill uses the distinct O-BF- prefix and does
     not advance the runtime sequence counter ‚ÄĒ do not reuse GenerateOrderNumber
     format in SQL.
     - Concurrency on a shared order (legs completing simultaneously):
     optimistic Version + bounded retry in recomputeOrder; Derive is pure so
     retries converge.
     - Partial billing: order goes Billed only when all active legs are
     Invoiced; partially-invoiced order stays Completed.
     - Idempotency of grouped invoice: anchor-BQI must be deterministic (first
     leg by pro number) so re-invoking returns the same invoice.
     - Rolled-back shipment create burns an order number ‚ÄĒ accepted, consistent
     with pro-number behavior.
     - Mixed-customer guard: CreateFromOrder rejects legs with differing
     CustomerID.

      682 +// buildInvoiceEntityForOrder builds a single grouped invoice 
          +covering every billable                                       
      683 +// leg of an order. Lines are appended per leg (each carrying 
          +its shipment identity)                                        
      684 +// and line numbers run continuously across legs. The header c
          +arries the order, not a                                       
      685 +// single shipment; the anchor billing-queue item keeps the he
          +ader's single-valued FK                                       
      686 +// and idempotency lookup working.                            
      687 +func (s *Service) buildInvoiceEntityForOrder(                 
      688 +  anchor *billingqueue.BillingQueueItem,                      
      689 +  ord *order.Order,                                           
      690 +  legs []*shipment.Shipment,                                  
      691 +  cus *customer.Customer,                                     
      692 +  control *tenant.BillingControl,                             
      693 +) *invoice.Invoice {                                          
      694 +  invoiceDate := timeutils.NowUnix()                          
      695 +  paymentTerm := resolvePaymentTerm(cus, control)             
      696 +  if paymentTerm == "" {                                      
      697 +    paymentTerm = invoice.PaymentTermNet30                    
      698 +  }                                                           
      699 +                                                              
      700 +  lines := make([]*invoice.InoviceLine, 0, len(legs))         
      701 +  nextLineNumber := 1                                         
      702 +  for _, leg := range legs {                                  
      703 +    legLines := buildInvoiceLinesForShipment(anchor.BillType, 
          +leg, nextLineNumber)                                          
      704 +    lines = append(lines, legLines...)                        
      705 +    nextLineNumber += len(legLines)                           
      706 +  }                                                           
      707 +                                                              
      708 +  entity := &invoice.Invoice{                                 
      709 +    OrganizationID:     anchor.OrganizationID,                
      710 +    BusinessUnitID:     anchor.BusinessUnitID,                
      711 +    BillingQueueItemID: anchor.ID,                            
      712 +    OrderID:            ord.ID,                               
      713 +    OrderNumber:        ord.OrderNumber,                      
      714 +    CustomerID:         cus.ID,                               
      715 +    Number:             anchor.Number,                        
      716 +    BillType:           anchor.BillType,                      
      717 +    Status:             invoice.StatusDraft,                  
      718 +    PaymentTerm:        paymentTerm,                          
      719 +    CurrencyCode:       billingCurrencyFromCustomer(cus),     
      720 +    InvoiceDate:        invoiceDate,                          
      721 +    DueDate:            invoice.DueDateFromPaymentTerm(invoice
          +Date, paymentTerm),                                           
      722 +    BillToName:         cus.Name,                             
      723 +    BillToCode:         cus.Code,                             
      724 +    BillToAddressLine1: cus.AddressLine1,                     
      725 +    BillToAddressLine2: cus.AddressLine2,                     
      726 +    BillToCity:         cus.City,                             
      727 +    BillToPostalCode:   cus.PostalCode,                       
      728 +    AppliedAmount:      decimal.Zero,                         
      729 +    SettlementStatus:   invoice.SettlementStatusUnpaid,       
      730 +    DisputeStatus:      invoice.DisputeStatusNone,            
      731 +    Lines:              lines,                                
      732 +  }                                                           
      733 +                                                              
      734 +  if cus.State != nil {                                       
      735 +    entity.BillToState = cus.State.Abbreviation               
      736 +    entity.BillToCountry = cus.State.CountryName              
      737 +  }                                                           
      738 +                                                              
      739 +  syncInvoiceTotalsFromLines(entity)                          
      740 +  entity.SyncMinorAmounts()                                   
      741 +                                                              
      742 +  return entity                                               
      743 +}                                                             
      744 +                                                              
      745  type adjustmentInvoiceContext struct {
      746    ReplacementLines   []*invoice.InoviceLine `json:"replacement
           Lines"`

           unt"`

      144 +// groupedInvoiceFromShipments resolves the single order share
          +d by the given legs and                                       
      145 +// delegates to CreateFromOrder. It rejects legs that are not 
          +all under one order.                                          
      146 +func (s *Service) groupedInvoiceFromShipments(                
      147 +  ctx context.Context,                                        
      148 +  req *servicesports.CreateInvoiceFromShipmentsRequest,       
      149 +  actor *servicesports.RequestActor,                          
      150 +) (*invoice.Invoice, error) {                                 
      151 +  var orderID pulid.ID                                        
      152 +  for _, shipmentID := range req.ShipmentIDs {                
      153 +    shp, err := s.shipmentRepo.GetByID(ctx, &repositories.GetS
          +hipmentByIDRequest{                                           
      154 +      ID:         shipmentID,                                 
      155 +      TenantInfo: req.TenantInfo,                             
      156 +    })                                                        
      157 +    if err != nil {                                           
      158 +      return nil, err                                         
      159 +    }                                                         
      160 +    if shp.OrderID.IsNil() {                                  
      161 +      return nil, errortypes.NewValidationError(              
      162 +        "shipmentIds",                                        
      163 +        errortypes.ErrInvalid,                                
      164 +        "Grouped invoicing requires every shipment to belong t
          +o an order",                                                  
      165 +      )                                                       
      166 +    }                                                         
      167 +    if orderID.IsNil() {                                      
      168 +      orderID = shp.OrderID                                   
      169 +    } else if orderID != shp.OrderID {                        
      170 +      return nil, errortypes.NewValidationError(              
      171 +        "shipmentIds",                                        
      172 +        errortypes.ErrInvalid,                                
      173 +        "All shipments in a grouped invoice must belong to the
          + same order",                                                 
      174 +      )                                                       
      175 +    }                                                         
      176 +  }                                                           
      177 +                                                              
      178 +  return s.CreateFromOrder(ctx, &servicesports.CreateInvoiceFr
          +omOrderRequest{                                               
      179 +    OrderID:    orderID,                                      
      180 +    TenantInfo: req.TenantInfo,                               
      181 +  }, actor)                                                   
      182 +}                                                             
      183 +                                                              
      184 +// CreateFromOrder issues a single grouped invoice covering ev
          +ery billable leg of an                                        
      185 +// order. Each billable leg gets its own approved billing-queu
          +e item (all carrying the                                      
      186 +// order id); the first is the anchor whose id backs the invoi
          +ce header's single-valued                                     
      187 +// FK and idempotency lookup.                                 
      188 +func (s *Service) CreateFromOrder(                            
      189 +  ctx context.Context,                                        
      190 +  req *servicesports.CreateInvoiceFromOrderRequest,           
      191 +  actor *servicesports.RequestActor,                          
      192 +) (*invoice.Invoice, error) {                                 
      193 +  if req == nil {                                             
      194 +    return nil, errortypes.NewValidationError("request", error
          +types.ErrRequired, "Request is required")                     
      195 +  }                                                           
      196 +  if actor == nil {                                           
      197 +    return nil, errortypes.NewValidationError("actor", errorty
          +pes.ErrRequired, "Actor is required")                         
      198 +  }                                                           
      199 +  if req.OrderID.IsNil() {                                    
      200 +    return nil, errortypes.NewValidationError("orderId", error
          +types.ErrRequired, "Order is required")                       
      201 +  }                                                           
      202 +                                                              
      203 +  ord, err := s.orderRepo.GetByID(ctx, repositories.GetOrderBy
          +IDRequest{                                                    
      204 +    ID:              req.OrderID,                             
      205 +    TenantInfo:      req.TenantInfo,                          
      206 +    IncludeShipment: true,                                    
      207 +  })                                                          
      208 +  if err != nil {                                             
      209 +    return nil, err                                           
      210 +  }                                                           
      211 +                                                              
      212 +  legs := make([]*shipment.Shipment, 0, len(ord.Shipments))   
      213 +  for _, leg := range ord.Shipments {                         
      214 +    if leg == nil {                                           
      215 +      continue                                                
      216 +    }                                                         
      217 +    if leg.Status != shipment.StatusReadyToInvoice && leg.Stat
          +us != shipment.StatusCompleted {                              
      218 +      continue                                                
      219 +    }                                                         
      220 +    if leg.CustomerID != ord.CustomerID {                     
      221 +      return nil, errortypes.NewValidationError(              
      222 +        "orderId",                                            
      223 +        errortypes.ErrInvalid,                                
      224 +        "All legs of a grouped invoice must share the order's 
          +customer",                                                    
      225 +      )                                                       
      226 +    }                                                         
      227 +                                                              
      228 +    exists, existErr := s.billingQueueRepo.ExistsByShipmentAnd
          +Type(ctx, req.TenantInfo, leg.ID, billingqueue.BillTypeInvoice
          +)                                                             
      229 +    if existErr != nil {                                      
      230 +      return nil, existErr                                    
      231 +    }                                                         
      232 +    if exists {                                               
      233 +      return nil, errortypes.NewConflictError(                
      234 +        "A billing queue item already exists for a leg of this
          + order",                                                      
      235 +      )                                                       
      236 +    }                                                         
      237 +                                                              
      238 +    full, legErr := s.shipmentRepo.GetByID(ctx, expandedShipme
          +ntByIDRequest(leg.ID, req.TenantInfo))

      247 +      "orderId",

          +e",

          +, req.TenantInfo.OrgID, req.TenantInfo.BuID, "", "")

      255 +    return nil, err

      266 +      BillType:       billingqueue.BillTypeInvoice,           
      267 +      Number:         number,                                 
      268 +    })

      270 +      return nil, itemErr                                     
      271 +    }                                                         
      272 +    if anchor == nil {                                        
      273 +      anchor = item                                           
      274 +    }                                                         
      275 +  }

      283 +    },                                                        
      284 +  })

      286 +    return nil, err                                           
      287 +  }

          +.OrgID)

      291 +    return nil, err                                           
      292 +  }

          +s, control)

          +iErr != nil {

      297 +  }

      312 +  )

          +reated)

      177 +// to Posted. Used when a grouped invoice posts so all of the 
          +order's leg items settle                                      
      178 +// together, not just the anchor. Returns the number of rows u
          +pdated.                                                       
      179 +func (r *repository) MarkPostedByOrderID(                     
      180 +  ctx context.Context,                                        
      181 +  tenantInfo pagination.TenantInfo,                           
      182 +  orderID pulid.ID,                                           
      183 +) (int64, error) {                                            
      184 +  if orderID.IsNil() {                                        
      185 +    return 0, nil

      190 +    Model((*billingqueue.BillingQueueItem)(nil)).             
      191 +    Where(bqi.OrderID.Eq(), orderID).

      203 +  if err != nil {                                             
      204 +    return 0, fmt.Errorf("rows affected: %w", err)            
      205 +  }                                                           
      206 +

      446 +// markInvoicedLegs flips every shipment billed by this invoic
          +e to Invoiced. For a                                          
      447 +// single-shipment invoice that is one leg; for a grouped (ord
          +er) invoice it is the set                                     
      448 +// of legs carried on the invoice lines. It returns the first 
          +leg for downstream                                            
      449 +// reconciliation notification.                               
      450 +func (s *Service) markInvoicedLegs(                           
      451 +  ctx context.Context,                                        
      452 +  entity *invoice.Invoice,                                    
      453 +  now int64,                                                  
      454 +  tenantInfo pagination.TenantInfo,                           
      455 +) (*shipment.Shipment, error) {                               
      456 +  legIDs := invoiceLegShipmentIDs(entity)                     
      457 +  if len(legIDs) == 0 {                                       
      458 +    return nil, nil                                           
      459 +  }                                                           
      460 +                                                              
      461 +  var primary *shipment.Shipment                              
      462 +  for _, legID := range legIDs {                              
      463 +    shp, err := s.shipmentRepo.GetByID(ctx, basicShipmentByIDR
          +equest(legID, tenantInfo))                                    
      464 +    if err != nil {                                           
      465 +      return nil, err                                         
      466 +    }                                                         
      467 +                                                              
      468 +    shp.Status = shipment.StatusInvoiced                      
      469 +    shp.BilledAt = &now                                       
      470 +    if _, err = s.shipmentRepo.UpdateDerivedState(ctx, shp); e
          +rr != nil {                                                   
      471 +      return nil, err                                         
      472 +    }                                                         
      473 +                                                              
      474 +    if primary == nil {                                       
      475 +      primary = shp                                           
      476 +    }                                                         
      477 +  }                                                           
      478 +                                                              
      479 +  return primary, nil                                         
      480 +}                                                             
      481 +                                                              
      482 +// invoiceLegShipmentIDs returns the distinct shipments billed
          + by an invoice, preferring                                    
      483 +// the per-line attribution (which covers grouped invoices) an
          +d falling back to the                                         
      484 +// header shipment id for legacy single-shipment invoices whos
          +e lines predate line-level                                    
      485 +// attribution.                                               
      486 +func invoiceLegShipmentIDs(entity *invoice.Invoice) []pulid.ID
          + {                                                            
      487 +  seen := make(map[pulid.ID]struct{}, len(entity.Lines))      
      488 +  ids := make([]pulid.ID, 0, len(entity.Lines))               
      489 +  for _, line := range entity.Lines {                         
      490 +    if line == nil || line.ShipmentID.IsNil() {               
      491 +      continue                                                
      492 +    }                                                         
      493 +    if _, ok := seen[line.ShipmentID]; ok {                   
      494 +      continue                                                
      495 +    }                                                         
      496 +    seen[line.ShipmentID] = struct{}{}                        
      497 +    ids = append(ids, line.ShipmentID)                        
      498 +  }                                                           
      499 +                                                              
      500 +  if len(ids) == 0 && !entity.ShipmentID.IsNil() {            
      501 +    ids = append(ids, entity.ShipmentID)                      
      502 +  }                                                           
      503 +                                                              
      504 +  return ids                                                  
      505 +}

      206 +func (s *Service) recomputeStatus(                            
      207 +  ctx context.Context,                                        
      208 +  tenantInfo pagination.TenantInfo,                           
      209 +  orderID pulid.ID,                                           
      210 +) error {                                                     
      211 +  ord, err := s.repo.GetByID(ctx, repositories.GetOrderByIDReq
          +uest{                                                         
      212 +    ID:         orderID,                                      
      213 +    TenantInfo: tenantInfo,                                   
      214 +  })

      216 +    return err                                                
      217 +  }                                                           
      218 +  if ord.Status == order.StatusClosed {                       
      219 +    return nil                                                
      220 +  }                                                           
      221 +                                                              
      222 +  statuses, err := s.repo.GetShipmentStatuses(ctx, tenantInfo,
          + orderID)                                                     
      223 +  if err != nil {                                             
      224 +    return err                                                
      225 +  }                                                           
      226 +                                                              
      227 +  next := order.Derive(statuses)                              
      228 +  if next == ord.Status {                                     
      229 +    return nil                                                
      230 +  }                                                           
      231 +                                                              
      232 +  _, err = s.repo.UpdateStatus(ctx, &repositories.UpdateOrderS
          +tatusRequest{                                                 
      233 +    TenantInfo: tenantInfo,                                   
      234 +    OrderID:    orderID,                                      
      235 +    Status:     next,                                         
      236 +    Version:    ord.Version,                                  
      237 +  })                                                          
      238 +  return err                                                  
      239 +}

‚óŹ Both done, tsc clean:

  - Orders now write via GraphQL, not REST ‚ÄĒ createOrder/updateOrder mutations
  (mapped through toOrderInput, with the derived status omitted); the panels use
  mutationFn instead of the REST url. I've saved this as a standing rule so all

  ownerId to the fragment.

  write (it's derived from the legs), so editing an order won't clobber its
  computed status. If you'd rather the form be able to set an initial status on
  create, say so and I'll add it to the input.

      348 +func (r *repository) CountShipmentsWithDifferentCustomer(     
      349 +  ctx context.Context,                                        
      350 +  tenantInfo pagination.TenantInfo,                           
      351 +  customerID pulid.ID,                                        
      352 +  shipmentIDs []pulid.ID,                                     
      353 +) (int64, error) {

      363 +    Where("customer_id != ?", customerID).                    
      364 +    Count(ctx)

      366 +    r.l.Error("failed to count shipments with different custom
          +er", zap.Error(err))

‚óŹ Both commits are on master (601b92042, c769a8444). The React Doctor hook
  flagged client warnings again (non-blocking) ‚ÄĒ say the word and I'll run
  react-doctor --staged --fail-on warning and clean them up.

  Here's a comment you can drop on #507 as a follow-up to your earlier reply:

  ---
  Update: this is now built. The Order aggregate we discussed as the extension
  path has landed on master (601b92042, c769a8444).

  What shipped

  - A commercial Order above shipment. An order owns the customer, quote
  (quoted/base), currency, order-level charges, and AR total; shipments stay the
  execution unit and gain a nullable order_id. Creating a plain shipment
  auto-creates a one-leg order behind it, and existing shipments were backfilled
  1:1, so nothing about single-truckload entry changes.
  - order ‚Üí many shipments. Attach existing shipments as legs; the order status
  derives from its legs (Draft ‚Üí Confirmed ‚Üí InProgress ‚Üí Completed ‚Üí Billed ‚Üí 
  Closed, plus Canceled).
  - One customer invoice over multiple legs. CreateFromShipments' old "grouped
  invoices are not supported yet" guard is gone ‚ÄĒ a grouped invoice now covers
  every billable leg, with each line attributed to its shipment, and posting
  settles all of the order's billing-queue items and marks every leg Invoiced.
  - Quoted/base + extra charges. Per-leg accessorials still live on the
  shipment; new order-level charges (customs brokerage, order-wide fuel, etc.)
  roll into the order total and appear as their own lines on the grouped
  invoice.
  - Order-level AR. The order total rolls up from legs + order charges as
  membership changes.

  Answering the original questions directly

  1‚Äď4. The recommended model is now the Order aggregate for commercial
  continuity ‚ÄĒ one quote/order/invoice/customer AR ‚ÄĒ with one shipment per
  executing leg underneath. For legs run by different legal entities, the
  existing inter-org EDI transfers still create/link those shipments; they now
  share the same order_id, giving them the commercial parent they previously
  lacked.
  5. The old consolidation_*/summary fields were load consolidation and remain
  separate; grouped billing is now a real, end-to-end feature on the order, not
  those placeholders.

  Deliberately deferred (as future domains, per the design write-up): a
  first-class Route aggregate with customs/border checkpoints, and per-leg 
  carrier/buy-side cost. Those bolt onto the order later.

  Design notes: docs/design/order-aggregate.md in the repo. Thanks for the
  thorough writeup ‚ÄĒ it mapped almost 1:1 to what we built.

  ---
  Want me to also fix the React Doctor warnings, or tweak the comment's
  tone/length?

‚óŹ TSC clean. The Order Charges add-row now uses react-hook-form properly:

  - A local useForm<OrderChargeFormValues> with
  zodResolver(orderChargeFormSchema) (schema lives in types/order.ts next to the
  order schema).
  - RHF-bound InputField (description) and NumberField (amount,
  decimalScale={2}, thousand separators, currency sideText).
  - Validation: description required, amount required and must be > 0 ‚ÄĒ the Add
  button enables off formState.isValid, and the fields surface the zod error
  messages.
  - On success the form resets; mutation still goes through the GraphQL
  addOrderCharge.

  The null as unknown as number default is the small wart of letting NumberField
  hold an empty (null) value against a schema whose output is a required number
  ‚ÄĒ the zodResolver(...) as Resolver<...> cast is the same pattern the
  accounting-control form uses. Want me to commit + push this along with the
  customer-filter change?
